The\n1597:         return value depends on the value of result_type.\n1598: \n1599:         When result_type is:\n1600:         - MULTI: Retrieves all rows using fetchmany(). Wraps in an iterator for\n1601:            chunked reads when supported.\n1602:         - SINGLE: Retrieves a single row using fetchone().\n1603:         - ROW_COUNT: Retrieves the number of rows in the result.\n1604:         - CURSOR: Runs the query, and returns the cursor object. Check for raw values,\n1685:         expressions, and fields with get_placeholder() defined in that order.\n1686: \n1687:         When field is None, consider the value raw and use it as the\n1688:         placeholder, with no corresponding parameters returned.\n1689:         \"\"\"\n1690:         if field is None:\n1691:             # A field value of None means the value is raw.\n1692:             sql, params = val, []\n1693:         elif hasattr(val, \"as_sql\"):\n1694:             # This is an expression, let's compile it.\n1695:             sql, params = self.compile(val)\n1696:         elif get_placeholder is not None:\n1697:             # Some fields (e.g. geo fields) need special munging before\n1698:             # they can be inserted.\n1699:             sql, params = get_placeholder(val, self, self.connection), [val]\n1700:         else:\n1701:             # Return the common case for the placeholder\n1702:             sql, params = \"%s\", [val]\n1703: \n1704:         # The following hook is only used by Oracle Spatial, which sometimes\n1705:         # needs to yield 'NULL' and [] as its placeholder and params instead\n1706:         # of '%s' and [None]. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01FLdoTX3QzJCEYEJiFWKSie","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I understand the flow. When `values_list()` is called with expressions:\n1. The expressions are passed to `_values()` as keyword arguments\n2. `_values()` calls `annotate()` to add them as annotations\n3. `_values()` calls `query.set_values(fields)` with the field names (from the expressions)\n4. `set_values()` sets `self.selected` which controls what gets selected\n\nThe key issue is that when `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called, it needs to find the first selected column from the model. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01JSCHULuDVZBudsJHwVZqwT","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I understand the complete bug:1. When `values_list()` is called with expression arguments like `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`, the expressions are annotated via `annotate()`.2. `set_values()` is called which creates `self.query.selected` with the field names/aliases in the order they appear in `values_list()`.3. In `get_select()` at lines 253-268, `select_fields` is calculated based on the assumption that model columns are at positions `len(self.query.extra_select)` to `len(self.query.extra_select) + len(cols)`.4. However, at lines 280-290, when `self.query.selected` is not None, the selected list is built by iterating through `self.query.selected.items()`, which can contain annotation expressions.5. The problem is that `select_fields` still points to the old indices where model columns are expected, but in the `selected` list built from `self.query.selected`, the annotation expressions might come first!6. When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called, at lines 1424-1425 and 1440, it tries to access `.target.model` on items at the indices in `select_fields`, but these might be annotation expressions which don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\nThe root cause is that:- `select_fields` is populated at lines 262-267 based on the positions in the default columns list- But when `self.query.selected` is not None, the actual positions of model columns in the select list can be different\n- The code at lines 1424-1425 and 1440 assumes all items in `select_fields` are Col objects with a `.target` attribute\n\nThe fix is to add a check to ensure that the expression has a `.target` attribute before accessing it. Alternatively, we could recalculate which select indices correspond to model field columns, but the simpler fix is to just check for the attribute.\n\n\nI should document this analysis Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405 and its nested helper functions\n- **django/db/models/query.py** — `values_list()` method at line 1369 and `_values()` at line 1355\n- **django/db/models/sql/query.py** — `set_values()` method at line 2492 (controls how field selection is built)\n- **django/db/models/expressions.py** — `Col` class at line 1287 (defines the `.target` attribute on column references)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User calls `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n\n2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/query.py:1369` — `values_list()` method processes the annotation expression and regular fields\n\n3. **Processed by**: `django/db/models/query.py:1355` — `_values()` converts expression arguments to annotations via `annotate()`\n\n4. **Then calls**: `django/db/models/sql/query.py:2492` — `set_values()` marks which fields are selected and sets `self.query.selected`\n\n5. **SQL generation in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:248` — `get_select()` method builds the select list using `self.query.selected`\n\n6. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:1405` — `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method attempts to determine which model columns are selected in order to apply the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Functions**:\n  - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405\n  - `_get_parent_klass_info()` (nested helper, line 1411)\n  - `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (nested helper, line 1430)\n- **Lines with bug**:\n  - Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`)\n\n**Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because of a mismatch between how `select_fields` is populated and how it's used:\n\n1. At lines 262-267 in `get_select()`, `select_fields` is calculated assuming model columns are at specific positions (from index `len(extra_select)` to `len(extra_select) + len(cols)`).\n\n2. This assumption is valid when `self.query.selected is None` (default behavior), because the select list is built as: extra_select items → model columns → annotation items (lines 271-278).\n\n3. However, when `values_list()` is called with expression arguments, `self.query.selected` is not None (line 280). The selected list is then built by iterating through `self.query.selected.items()` (lines 280-290), which returns items in the order they appear in the dictionary. **The annotation expressions can appear before model field columns in this dictionary**.\n\n4. When the select list is rebuilt from `self.query.selected` at lines 280-290, annotation expressions (like `Concat()`) are added to the select list. These are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects, so they **do not have a `.target` attribute**.\n\n5. The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method uses `select_fields` to find which selected items correspond to model columns by checking if `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model` (lines 1424-1425, 1440).\n\n6. **The crash occurs** because when `select_fields` contains an index pointing to an annotation expression (which doesn't have `.target`), accessing `.target.model` raises an `AttributeError`.\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nWhen `values_list(Concat(...), \"name\")` is called:\n- The `Concat` expression becomes an annotation\n- `set_values()` creates `self.query.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"name\": 0}` (or similar)\n- In `get_select()`, this dictionary is iterated, adding the expression first, then the field\n- But `select_fields` still points to indices assuming the old order\n- When annotation expressions are added to the select list, `select_fields` indices now point to expressions instead of columns\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to add `hasattr(expr, \"target\")` checks before accessing the `.target` attribute. This follows the pattern already used at line 212 in the same file:\n\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(expr, \"target\")\n    and expr.target.primary_key\n    and self.connection.features.allows_group_by_selected_pks_on_model(\n        expr.target.model\n    )\n):\n```\n\n### Diff for `_get_parent_klass_info()` (lines 1419-1427):\n\n```diff\n             \"select_fields\": [\n                 select_index\n                 for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                 # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n                 if (\n-                    self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                    or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and (\n+                        self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                        or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                    )\n                 )\n             ],\n```\n\n### Diff for `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (lines 1439-1441):\n\n```diff\n         def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n             \"\"\"\n             Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n             don't lock a model.\n\n             select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n             from the parent models.\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+                ):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\nThe bug is a subtle interaction between two features:\n\n1. **Recent `values_list()` enhancement** (support for expression arguments) changed the order of items in the select clause. Previously, when `values()` or `values_list()` was called, it would preserve the default order of model columns first, then annotations.\n\n2. **The `select_for_update(of=...)` feature** relies on identifying which selected items correspond to model columns so it can lock them in the FOR UPDATE OF clause. The implementation assumes that all items at indices in `select_fields` are `Col` objects representing model field columns.\n\nThe fix properly guards against accessing `.target` on non-Col expressions. When an annotation expression is encountered, it's skipped (because annotations don't represent model columns), and the search continues for the first actual model column. This preserves the correct behavior while preventing the crash.\n\nThe fix is minimal and correct because:\n- It only adds defensive checks\n- It maintains backward compatibility (existing code paths unaffected)\n- It follows the established pattern in the same file (line 212)\n- It correctly handles the case where `select_fields` points to annotation expressions (which should be skipped when looking for model columns)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1277,"cache_read_input_tokens":81238,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1277},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1c1911d9-5c55-4b30-9b2c-20331a82701f","uuid":"342a735c-ac5d-472b-970f-84a60427dba4"}

Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405 and its nested helper functions\n- **django/db/models/query.py** — `values_list()` method at line 1369 and `_values()` at line 1355\n- **django/db/models/sql/query.py** — `set_values()` method at line 2492 (controls how field selection is built)\n- **django/db/models/expressions.py** — `Col` class at line 1287 (defines the `.target` attribute on column references)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User calls `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n\n2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/query.py:1369` — `values_list()` method processes the annotation expression and regular fields\n\n3. **Processed by**: `django/db/models/query.py:1355` — `_values()` converts expression arguments to annotations via `annotate()`\n\n4. **Then calls**: `django/db/models/sql/query.py:2492` — `set_values()` marks which fields are selected and sets `self.query.selected`\n\n5. **SQL generation in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:248` — `get_select()` method builds the select list using `self.query.selected`\n\n6. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:1405` — `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method attempts to determine which model columns are selected in order to apply the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Functions**:\n  - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405\n  - `_get_parent_klass_info()` (nested helper, line 1411)\n  - `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (nested helper, line 1430)\n- **Lines with bug**:\n  - Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`)\n\n**Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because of a mismatch between how `select_fields` is populated and how it's used:\n\n1. At lines 262-267 in `get_select()`, `select_fields` is calculated assuming model columns are at specific positions (from index `len(extra_select)` to `len(extra_select) + len(cols)`).\n\n2. This assumption is valid when `self.query.selected is None` (default behavior), because the select list is built as: extra_select items → model columns → annotation items (lines 271-278).\n\n3. However, when `values_list()` is called with expression arguments, `self.query.selected` is not None (line 280). The selected list is then built by iterating through `self.query.selected.items()` (lines 280-290), which returns items in the order they appear in the dictionary. **The annotation expressions can appear before model field columns in this dictionary**.\n\n4. When the select list is rebuilt from `self.query.selected` at lines 280-290, annotation expressions (like `Concat()`) are added to the select list. These are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects, so they **do not have a `.target` attribute**.\n\n5. The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method uses `select_fields` to find which selected items correspond to model columns by checking if `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model` (lines 1424-1425, 1440).\n\n6. **The crash occurs** because when `select_fields` contains an index pointing to an annotation expression (which doesn't have `.target`), accessing `.target.model` raises an `AttributeError`.\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nWhen `values_list(Concat(...), \"name\")` is called:\n- The `Concat` expression becomes an annotation\n- `set_values()` creates `self.query.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"name\": 0}` (or similar)\n- In `get_select()`, this dictionary is iterated, adding the expression first, then the field\n- But `select_fields` still points to indices assuming the old order\n- When annotation expressions are added to the select list, `select_fields` indices now point to expressions instead of columns\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to add `hasattr(expr, \"target\")` checks before accessing the `.target` attribute. This follows the pattern already used at line 212 in the same file:\n\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(expr, \"target\")\n    and expr.target.primary_key\n    and self.connection.features.allows_group_by_selected_pks_on_model(\n        expr.target.model\n    )\n):\n```\n\n### Diff for `_get_parent_klass_info()` (lines 1419-1427):\n\n```diff\n             \"select_fields\": [\n                 select_index\n                 for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                 # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n                 if (\n-                    self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                    or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and (\n+                        self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                        or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                    )\n                 )\n             ],\n```\n\n### Diff for `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (lines 1439-1441):\n\n```diff\n         def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n             \"\"\"\n             Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n             don't lock a model.\n\n             select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n             from the parent models.\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+                ):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\nThe bug is a subtle interaction between two features:\n\n1. **Recent `values_list()` enhancement** (support for expression arguments) changed the order of items in the select clause. Previously, when `values()` or `values_list()` was called, it would preserve the default order of model columns first, then annotations.\n\n2. **The `select_for_update(of=...)` feature** relies on identifying which selected items correspond to model columns so it can lock them in the FOR UPDATE OF clause. The implementation assumes that all items at indices in `select_fields` are `Col` objects representing model field columns.\n\nThe fix properly guards against accessing `.target` on non-Col expressions. When an annotation expression is encountered, it's skipped (because annotations don't represent model columns), and the search continues for the first actual model column. This preserves the correct behavior while preventing the crash.\n\nThe fix is minimal and correct because:\n- It only adds defensive checks\n- It maintains backward compatibility (existing code paths unaffected)\n- It follows the established pattern in the same file (line 212)\n- It correctly handles the case where `select_fields` points to annotation expressions (which should be skipped when looking for model columns)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":71,"oldLines":18,"newStart":71,"newLines":22,"lines":[" ):"," ```"," ","-### Diff for `_get_parent_klass_info()` (lines 1419-1427):","+### Implementation"," ","+There are two locations in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` that need fixes:","+","+#### Fix 1: `_get_parent_klass_info()` function (lines 1419-1427)","+"," ```diff","              \"select_fields\": [","                  select_index","                  for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]","                  # Previously, when `values()` or `values_list()` was called, it would preserve the default order of model columns first, then annotations.\n\n2. **The `select_for_update(of=...)` feature** relies on identifying which selected items correspond to model columns so it can lock them in the FOR UPDATE OF clause. Arguments: `Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\"))` and `\"born\"`\n   - The Concat expression is converted to a keyword argument via naming\n\n2. **`_values()` is called** (line 1355 in query.py)\n   - The expression keyword arguments are passed to `annotate()`, creating annotations\n   - `query.set_values([field_names])` is called with field names in the order: `[\"concat1\", \"born\"]`\n\n3. **`set_values()` is called** (line 2492 in query.py)\n   - Sets `self.query.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"born\": 0}` (or similar dict)\n   - This marks which fields should be selected and in what order\n\n4. **`get_select()` is called** (line 248 in compiler.py)\n   - Line 253: `self.query.default_cols = False` (because values() was used)\n   - Lines 262-267: `select_fields = [0, 1]` (range starting from `len(extra_select)`)\n   - Lines 280-290: Builds `selected` list by iterating `self.query.selected.items()`\n     - First item: `(\"concat1\", Concat(...))` → added to selected\n     - Second item: `(\"born\", 0)` → gets replaced with `cols[0]` (the \"born\" column)\n   - Lines 292-295: Builds final `self.select` list:\n     - `self.select[0] = (Concat(...), \"concat1\")`\n     - `self.select[1] = (Col(...), None)`\n\n5. **`get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called** (line 1405 in compiler.py)\n   - Tries to find the first selected column from the Person model to apply FOR UPDATE OF\n   - `select_fields = [0, 1]` (from step 4)\n   - For `select_fields[0] = 0`:\n     - Accesses `self.select[0][0]` → gets the `Concat(...)` expression\n     - **Attempts to access `.target` attribute** → CRASH! `Concat` has no `.target` attribute\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nThe root cause is **inconsistent indexing assumptions**:\n\n- **`select_fields` calculation** (line 264-266): Assumes model columns are at indices `len(extra_select)` through `len(extra_select) + len(cols)`\n- **`select` list construction when `self.query.selected` is not None** (lines 280-290): Uses the order from `self.query.selected.items()`, which can have annotations before model columns\n\nWhen `values_list()` with expression arguments is used, the expression dictionary order changes, causing annotation expressions to appear at indices that `select_fields` expects model columns to be.\n\n### Why the Existing Code Fails\n\nThe code at lines 1424-1425 and 1440 makes an unsafe assumption:\n```python\nif self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n```\n\nThis assumes:\n1. Every item in `self.select` at an index in `select_fields` is a `Col` object\n2. All `Col` objects have a `.target` attribute\n\nHowever, when annotation expressions are present, these assumptions fail:\n- Annotation expressions (Concat, F, Case, etc.) are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects\n- Expression objects do not have a `.target` attribute\n\n### Why the Fix Works\n\nThe fix adds a defensive check:\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n):\n```\n\nThis properly handles both cases:\n1. **When select_index points to a Col object**: The `hasattr()` check passes, and the model comparison works correctly\n2. **When select_index points to an annotation Expression**: The `hasattr()` check fails, the expression is skipped, and the loop continues looking for an actual model column\n\nThis is correct behavior because:\n- Annotation expressions don't represent model columns that can be locked with FOR UPDATE OF\n- The function is specifically looking for \"the first selected **column** from a model\" (emphasis from docstring at line 1432)\n- Skipping annotation expressions correctly focuses on finding model field columns\n\nThe fix is minimal and correct because:\n- It only adds defensive checks\n- It maintains backward compatibility (existing code paths unaffected)\n- It follows the established pattern in the same file (line 212)\n- It correctly handles the case where `select_fields` points to annotation expressions (which should be skipped when looking for model columns)"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":2,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1444,"cache_read_input_tokens":86511,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1444},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1c1911d9-5c55-4b30-9b2c-20331a82701f","uuid":"07f04494-6696-4041-bfdf-8d8aa03e183a"}

Previously, when `values()` or `values_list()` was called, it would preserve the default order of model columns first, then annotations.\n\n2. **The `select_for_update(of=...)` feature** relies on identifying which selected items correspond to model columns so it can lock them in the FOR UPDATE OF clause. Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405 and its nested helper functions\n- **django/db/models/query.py** — `values_list()` method at line 1369 and `_values()` at line 1355\n- **django/db/models/sql/query.py** — `set_values()` method at line 2492 (controls how field selection is built)\n- **django/db/models/expressions.py** — `Col` class at line 1287 (defines the `.target` attribute on column references)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User calls `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n\n2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/query.py:1369` — `values_list()` method processes the annotation expression and regular fields\n\n3. **Processed by**: `django/db/models/query.py:1355` — `_values()` converts expression arguments to annotations via `annotate()`\n\n4. **Then calls**: `django/db/models/sql/query.py:2492` — `set_values()` marks which fields are selected and sets `self.query.selected`\n\n5. **SQL generation in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:248` — `get_select()` method builds the select list using `self.query.selected`\n\n6. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:1405` — `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method attempts to determine which model columns are selected in order to apply the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Functions**:\n  - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405\n  - `_get_parent_klass_info()` (nested helper, line 1411)\n  - `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (nested helper, line 1430)\n- **Lines with bug**:\n  - Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`)\n\n**Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because of a mismatch between how `select_fields` is populated and how it's used:\n\n1. At lines 262-267 in `get_select()`, `select_fields` is calculated assuming model columns are at specific positions (from index `len(extra_select)` to `len(extra_select) + len(cols)`).\n\n2. This assumption is valid when `self.query.selected is None` (default behavior), because the select list is built as: extra_select items → model columns → annotation items (lines 271-278).\n\n3. However, when `values_list()` is called with expression arguments, `self.query.selected` is not None (line 280). The selected list is then built by iterating through `self.query.selected.items()` (lines 280-290), which returns items in the order they appear in the dictionary. **The annotation expressions can appear before model field columns in this dictionary**.\n\n4. When the select list is rebuilt from `self.query.selected` at lines 280-290, annotation expressions (like `Concat()`) are added to the select list. These are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects, so they **do not have a `.target` attribute**.\n\n5. The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method uses `select_fields` to find which selected items correspond to model columns by checking if `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model` (lines 1424-1425, 1440).\n\n6. **The crash occurs** because when `select_fields` contains an index pointing to an annotation expression (which doesn't have `.target`), accessing `.target.model` raises an `AttributeError`.\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nWhen `values_list(Concat(...), \"name\")` is called:\n- The `Concat` expression becomes an annotation\n- `set_values()` creates `self.query.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"name\": 0}` (or similar)\n- In `get_select()`, this dictionary is iterated, adding the expression first, then the field\n- But `select_fields` still points to indices assuming the old order\n- When annotation expressions are added to the select list, `select_fields` indices now point to expressions instead of columns\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to add `hasattr(expr, \"target\")` checks before accessing the `.target` attribute. This follows the pattern already used at line 212 in the same file:\n\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(expr, \"target\")\n    and expr.target.primary_key\n    and self.connection.features.allows_group_by_selected_pks_on_model(\n        expr.target.model\n    )\n):\n```\n\n### Implementation\n\nThere are two locations in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` that need fixes:\n\n#### Fix 1: `_get_parent_klass_info()` function (lines 1419-1427)\n\n```diff\n             \"select_fields\": [\n                 select_index\n                 for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                 # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n                 if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and (\n-                    self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                    or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                        self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                        or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                    )\n                 )\n             ],\n```\n\n#### Fix 2: `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` function (lines 1439-1441)\n\n```diff\n         def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n             \"\"\"\n             Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n             don't lock a model.\n\n             select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n             from the parent models.\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+                ):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\nThe bug is a subtle interaction between two features:\n\n1. **Recent `values_list()` enhancement** (support for expression arguments) changed the order of items in the select clause. Previously, when `values()` or `values_list()` was called, it would preserve the default order of model columns first, then annotations.\n\n2. **The `select_for_update(of=...)` feature** relies on identifying which selected items correspond to model columns so it can lock them in the FOR UPDATE OF clause. The implementation assumes that all items at indices in `select_fields` are `Col` objects representing model field columns.\n\nThe fix properly guards against accessing `.target` on non-Col expressions. When an annotation expression is encountered, it's skipped (because annotations don't represent model columns), and the search continues for the first actual model column. This preserves the correct behavior while preventing the crash.\n\nThe fix is minimal and correct because:\n- It only adds defensive checks\n- It maintains backward compatibility (existing code paths unaffected)\n- It follows the established pattern in the same file (line 212)\n- It correctly handles the case where `select_fields` points to annotation expressions (which should be skipped when looking for model columns)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":117,"oldLines":14,"newStart":117,"newLines":96,"lines":[" "," ## Analysis"," ","-The bug is a subtle interaction between two features:","+### The Bug Manifestation"," ","-1. **Recent `values_list()` enhancement** (support for expression arguments) changed the order of items in the select clause. Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** — Entry point `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405 and its nested helper functions\n- **django/db/models/query.py** — `values_list()` method at line 1369 and `_values()` at line 1355\n- **django/db/models/sql/query.py** — `set_values()` method at line 2492 (controls how field selection is built)\n- **django/db/models/expressions.py** — `Col` class at line 1287 (defines the `.target` attribute on column references)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: User calls `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\")`\n\n2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/query.py:1369` — `values_list()` method processes the annotation expression and regular fields\n\n3. **Processed by**: `django/db/models/query.py:1355` — `_values()` converts expression arguments to annotations via `annotate()`\n\n4. **Then calls**: `django/db/models/sql/query.py:2492` — `set_values()` marks which fields are selected and sets `self.query.selected`\n\n5. **SQL generation in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:248` — `get_select()` method builds the select list using `self.query.selected`\n\n6. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:1405` — `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method attempts to determine which model columns are selected in order to apply the FOR UPDATE OF clause\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Functions**:\n  - `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` at line 1405\n  - `_get_parent_klass_info()` (nested helper, line 1411)\n  - `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (nested helper, line 1430)\n- **Lines with bug**:\n  - Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`)\n\n**Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because of a mismatch between how `select_fields` is populated and how it's used:\n\n1. At lines 262-267 in `get_select()`, `select_fields` is calculated assuming model columns are at specific positions (from index `len(extra_select)` to `len(extra_select) + len(cols)`).\n\n2. This assumption is valid when `self.query.selected is None` (default behavior), because the select list is built as: extra_select items → model columns → annotation items (lines 271-278).\n\n3. However, when `values_list()` is called with expression arguments, `self.query.selected` is not None (line 280). The selected list is then built by iterating through `self.query.selected.items()` (lines 280-290), which returns items in the order they appear in the dictionary. **The annotation expressions can appear before model field columns in this dictionary**.\n\n4. When the select list is rebuilt from `self.query.selected` at lines 280-290, annotation expressions (like `Concat()`) are added to the select list. These are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects, so they **do not have a `.target` attribute**.\n\n5. The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method uses `select_fields` to find which selected items correspond to model columns by checking if `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model` (lines 1424-1425, 1440).\n\n6. **The crash occurs** because when `select_fields` contains an index pointing to an annotation expression (which doesn't have `.target`), accessing `.target.model` raises an `AttributeError`.\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nWhen `values_list(Concat(...), \"name\")` is called:\n- The `Concat` expression becomes an annotation\n- `set_values()` creates `self.query.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"name\": 0}` (or similar)\n- In `get_select()`, this dictionary is iterated, adding the expression first, then the field\n- But `select_fields` still points to indices assuming the old order\n- When annotation expressions are added to the select list, `select_fields` indices now point to expressions instead of columns\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is to add `hasattr(expr, \"target\")` checks before accessing the `.target` attribute. This follows the pattern already used at line 212 in the same file:\n\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(expr, \"target\")\n    and expr.target.primary_key\n    and self.connection.features.allows_group_by_selected_pks_on_model(\n        expr.target.model\n    )\n):\n```\n\n### Implementation\n\nThere are two locations in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` that need fixes:\n\n#### Fix 1: `_get_parent_klass_info()` function (lines 1419-1427)\n\n```diff\n             \"select_fields\": [\n                 select_index\n                 for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                 # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n                 if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and (\n-                    self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                    or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                        self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                        or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                    )\n                 )\n             ],\n```\n\n#### Fix 2: `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` function (lines 1439-1441)\n\n```diff\n         def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n             \"\"\"\n             Find the first selected column from a model. If it doesn't exist,\n             don't lock a model.\n\n             select_fields is filled recursively, so it also contains fields\n             from the parent models.\n             \"\"\"\n             concrete_model = klass_info[\"model\"]._meta.concrete_model\n             for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:\n-                if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n+                if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n+                ):\n                     return self.select[select_index][0]\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug Manifestation\n\nWhen executing:\n```python\nPerson.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n    Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n)\n```\n\nThe error occurs:\n```\nAttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'\n```\n\nThis happens at line 1440 or 1424 when the code tries to access `.target.model` on an annotation expression.\n\n### Step-by-Step Execution Trace\n\n1. **`values_list()` is called** (line 1369 in query.py)\n   - Arguments: `Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\"))` and `\"born\"`\n   - The Concat expression is converted to a keyword argument via naming\n\n2. **`_values()` is called** (line 1355 in query.py)\n   - The expression keyword arguments are passed to `annotate()`, creating annotations\n   - `query.set_values([field_names])` is called with field names in the order: `[\"concat1\", \"born\"]`\n\n3. **`set_values()` is called** (line 2492 in query.py)\n   - Sets `self.query.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"born\": 0}` (or similar dict)\n   - This marks which fields should be selected and in what order\n\n4. **`get_select()` is called** (line 248 in compiler.py)\n   - Line 253: `self.query.default_cols = False` (because values() was used)\n   - Lines 262-267: `select_fields = [0, 1]` (range starting from `len(extra_select)`)\n   - Lines 280-290: Builds `selected` list by iterating `self.query.selected.items()`\n     - First item: `(\"concat1\", Concat(...))` → added to selected\n     - Second item: `(\"born\", 0)` → gets replaced with `cols[0]` (the \"born\" column)\n   - Lines 292-295: Builds final `self.select` list:\n     - `self.select[0] = (Concat(...), \"concat1\")`\n     - `self.select[1] = (Col(...), None)`\n\n5. **`get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` is called** (line 1405 in compiler.py)\n   - Tries to find the first selected column from the Person model to apply FOR UPDATE OF\n   - `select_fields = [0, 1]` (from step 4)\n   - For `select_fields[0] = 0`:\n     - Accesses `self.select[0][0]` → gets the `Concat(...)` expression\n     - **Attempts to access `.target` attribute** → CRASH! `Concat` has no `.target` attribute\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nThe root cause is **inconsistent indexing assumptions**:\n\n- **`select_fields` calculation** (line 264-266): Assumes model columns are at indices `len(extra_select)` through `len(extra_select) + len(cols)`\n- **`select` list construction when `self.query.selected` is not None** (lines 280-290): Uses the order from `self.query.selected.items()`, which can have annotations before model columns\n\nWhen `values_list()` with expression arguments is used, the expression dictionary order changes, causing annotation expressions to appear at indices that `select_fields` expects model columns to be.\n\n### Why the Existing Code Fails\n\nThe code at lines 1424-1425 and 1440 makes an unsafe assumption:\n```python\nif self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n```\n\nThis assumes:\n1. Every item in `self.select` at an index in `select_fields` is a `Col` object\n2. All `Col` objects have a `.target` attribute\n\nHowever, when annotation expressions are present, these assumptions fail:\n- Annotation expressions (Concat, F, Case, etc.) are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects\n- Expression objects do not have a `.target` attribute\n\n### Why the Fix Works\n\nThe fix adds a defensive check:\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n):\n```\n\nThis properly handles both cases:\n1. **When select_index points to a Col object**: The `hasattr()` check passes, and the model comparison works correctly\n2. **When select_index points to an annotation Expression**: The `hasattr()` check fails, the expression is skipped, and the loop continues looking for an actual model column\n\nThis is correct behavior because:\n- Annotation expressions don't represent model columns that can be locked with FOR UPDATE OF\n- The function is specifically looking for \"the first selected **column** from a model\" (emphasis from docstring at line 1432)\n- Skipping annotation expressions correctly focuses on finding model field columns\n\nThe fix is minimal and correct because:\n- It only adds defensive checks\n- It maintains backward compatibility (existing code paths unaffected)\n- It follows the established pattern in the same file (line 212)\n- It correctly handles the case where `select_fields` points to annotation expressions (which should be skipped when looking for model columns)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":212,"oldLines":3,"newStart":212,"newLines":17,"lines":[" - This assumption is valid when `self.query.selected is None` (default behavior), because the select list is built as: extra_select items → model columns → annotation items (lines 271-278).\n    42→\n    43→3. However, when `values_list()` is called with expression arguments, `self.query.selected` is not None (line 280). The selected list is then built by iterating through `self.query.selected.items()` (lines 280-290), which returns items in the order they appear in the dictionary. **The annotation expressions can appear before model field columns in this dictionary**.\n    44→\n    45→4. When the select list is rebuilt from `self.query.selected` at lines 280-290, annotation expressions (like `Concat()`) are added to the select list. These are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects, so they **do not have a `.target` attribute**.\n    46→\n    47→5. The `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method uses `select_fields` to find which selected items correspond to model columns by checking if `self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model` (lines 1424-1425, 1440).\n    48→\n    49→6. **The crash occurs** because when `select_fields` contains an index pointing to an annotation expression (which doesn't have `.target`), accessing `.target.model` raises an `AttributeError`.\n    50→\n    51→### Why This Happens\n    52→\n    53→When `values_list(Concat(...), \"name\")` is called:\n    54→- The `Concat` expression becomes an annotation\n    55→- `set_values()` creates `self.query.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"name\": 0}` (or similar)\n    56→- In `get_select()`, this dictionary is iterated, adding the expression first, then the field\n    57→- But `select_fields` still points to indices assuming the old order\n    58→- When annotation expressions are added to the select list, `select_fields` indices now point to expressions instead of columns\n    59→\n    60→## Proposed Fix\n    61→\n    62→The fix is to add `hasattr(expr, \"target\")` checks before accessing the `.target` attribute. `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects\n   189→- Expression objects do not have a `.target` attribute\n   190→\n   191→### Why the Fix Works\n   192→\n   193→The fix adds a defensive check:\n   194→```python\n   195→if (\n   196→    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n   197→    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n   198→):\n   199→```\n   200→\n   201→This properly handles both cases:\n   202→1. **When select_index points to a Col object**: The `hasattr()` check passes, and the model comparison works correctly\n   203→2. **When select_index points to an annotation Expression**: The `hasattr()` check fails, the expression is skipped, and the loop continues looking for an actual model column\n   204→\n   205→This is correct behavior because:\n   206→- Annotation expressions don't represent model columns that can be locked with FOR UPDATE OF\n   207→- The function is specifically looking for \"the first selected **column** from a model\" (emphasis from docstring at line 1432)\n   208→- Skipping annotation expressions correctly focuses on finding model field columns\n   209→\n   210→The fix is minimal and correct because:\n   211→- It only adds defensive checks\n   212→- It maintains backward compatibility (existing code paths unaffected)\n   213→- It follows the established pattern in the same file (line 212)\n   214→- It correctly handles the case where `select_fields` points to annotation expressions (which should be skipped when looking for model columns)\n   215→\n   216→---\n   217→\n   218→## Summary\n   219→\n   220→**The Problem**: When `select_for_update(of=(\"self\",))` is combined with `values_list()` containing annotation expressions, the code crashes with `AttributeError` because it tries to access `.target.model` on annotation expressions that don't have a `.target` attribute.\n   221→\n   222→**The Root Cause**: The `select_fields` index calculation assumes model columns are at specific positions in the select list. However, when `values_list()` with expression arguments is used, annotation expressions can appear before model columns, causing `select_fields` indices to point to expressions instead of Col objects.\n   223→\n   224→**The Solution**: Add `hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")` checks before accessing `.target.model` in two places:\n   225→1. Line 1424-1425 in `_get_parent_klass_info()`\n   226→2. Line 1424-1425 (in `_get_parent_klass_info()`)\n  - Line 1440 (in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`)\n\n**Explanation**:\n\nThe bug occurs because of a mismatch between how `select_fields` is populated and how it's used:\n\n1. This follows the pattern already used at line 212 in the same file:\n\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(expr, \"target\")\n    and expr.target.primary_key\n    and self.connection.features.allows_group_by_selected_pks_on_model(\n        expr.target.model\n    )\n):\n```\n\n### Implementation\n\nThere are two locations in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` that need fixes:\n\n#### Fix 1: `_get_parent_klass_info()` function (lines 1419-1427)\n\n```diff\n             \"select_fields\": [\n                 select_index\n                 for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n                 # Selected columns from a model or its parents.\n                 if (\n+                    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n+                    and (\n-                    self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n-                    or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                        self.select[select_index][0].target.model == parent_model\n+                        or self.select[select_index][0].target.model in all_parents\n+                    )\n                 )\n             ],\n```\n\n#### Fix 2: `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` function (lines 1439-1441)\n\n```diff\n         def _get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info):\n             \"\"\"\n             Find the first selected column from a model. `select_fields = [0, 1]` (from step 4)\n   - For `select_fields[0] = 0`:\n     - Accesses `self.select[0][0]` → gets the `Concat(...)` expression\n     - **Attempts to access `.target` attribute** → CRASH! `Concat` has no `.target` attribute\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nThe root cause is **inconsistent indexing assumptions**:\n\n- **`select_fields` calculation** (line 264-266): Assumes model columns are at indices `len(extra_select)` through `len(extra_select) + len(cols)`\n- **`select` list construction when `self.query.selected` is not None** (lines 280-290): Uses the order from `self.query.selected.items()`, which can have annotations before model columns\n\nWhen `values_list()` with expression arguments is used, the expression dictionary order changes, causing annotation expressions to appear at indices that `select_fields` expects model columns to be.\n\n### Why the Existing Code Fails\n\nThe code at lines 1424-1425 and 1440 makes an unsafe assumption:\n```python\nif self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n```\n\nThis assumes:\n1. Every item in `self.select` at an index in `select_fields` is a `Col` object\n2. All `Col` objects have a `.target` attribute\n\nHowever, when annotation expressions are present, these assumptions fail:\n- Annotation expressions (Concat, F, Case, etc.) are `Expression` objects, not `Col` objects\n- Expression objects do not have a `.target` attribute\n\n### Why the Fix Works\n\nThe fix adds a defensive check:\n```python\nif (\n    hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")\n    and self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model\n):\n```\n\nThis properly handles both cases:\n1. **When select_index points to a Col object**: The `hasattr()` check passes, and the model comparison works correctly\n2. **When select_index points to an annotation Expression**: The `hasattr()` check fails, the expression is skipped, and the loop continues looking for an actual model column\n\nThis is correct behavior because:\n- Annotation expressions don't represent model columns that can be locked with FOR UPDATE OF\n- The function is specifically looking for \"the first selected **column** from a model\" (emphasis from docstring at line 1432)\n- Skipping annotation expressions correctly focuses on finding model field columns\n\nThe fix is minimal and correct because:\n- It only adds defensive checks\n- It maintains backward compatibility (existing code paths unaffected)\n- It follows the established pattern in the same file (line 212)\n- It correctly handles the case where `select_fields` points to annotation expressions (which should be skipped when looking for model columns)\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\n**The Problem**: When `select_for_update(of=(\"self\",))` is combined with `values_list()` containing annotation expressions, the code crashes with `AttributeError` because it tries to access `.target.model` on annotation expressions that don't have a `.target` attribute.\n\n**The Root Cause**: The `select_fields` index calculation assumes model columns are at specific positions in the select list. However, when `values_list()` with expression arguments is used, annotation expressions can appear before model columns, causing `select_fields` indices to point to expressions instead of Col objects.\n\n**The Solution**: Add `hasattr(self.select[select_index][0], \"target\")` checks before accessing `.target.model` in two places:\n1. Line 1424-1425 in `_get_parent_klass_info()`\n2. Line 1440 in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`\n\nThis defensive check follows the existing pattern at line 212 and properly skips annotation expressions while finding model columns for the FOR UPDATE OF clause.\n","numLines":229,"startLine":1,"totalLines":229}}}
